The <foreign lang="ar">حُدُود</foreign> of God are of two kinds: first, those <hi rend="ital">ordinances prescribed to men</hi> (T, Mgh, L) <hi rend="ital">respecting eatables and drinkables and marriages</hi> &amp;c.; <hi rend="ital">what are lawful thereof and what are unlawful:</hi> (T, L:) the second kind, <hi rend="ital">castigations,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">punishments, prescribed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">appointed, to be inflicted upon him who does that which he has been forbidden to do;</hi> (T, Mgh, L;) as the <foreign lang="ar">حدّ</foreign> of the thief, which is the cutting off of his right hand for stealing a thing of the value of a quarter of a deenár or more; and that of the fornicator or fornicatress, which is flogging with a hundred stripes and banishment for a year; and that of the adulterer or adulteress, which is stoning; and that of the person who [falsely] charges an honest or a married woman with adultery, which is flogging with eighty stripes [as is also that of the person who has committed the crime of drunkenness]: (T, L:) the first kind are called <foreign lang="ar">حدود</foreign> because they denote limits which God has forbidden to transgress: the second, because they prevent one's committing again those acts for which they are appointed as punishments; (T, Mgh, L;) or because the limits thereof are determined: (Mgh:) the latter kind of <foreign lang="ar">حدّ</foreign> is also explained as being <hi rend="ital">that</hi> [<hi rend="ital">castigation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">punishment,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">which prevents the criminal from returning to his crime, and prevents others from committing his crime.</hi> (L, K. *) <foreign lang="ar">لَوْ رَأَيْتَهُ عَلَى حَدٍّ</foreign>, in a saying of ' Omar, means <hi rend="ital">Hadst thou seen him engaged in an affair requiring the infliction of the</hi>
